<div id="review_592919889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592919889" />
    <a title="Aurian Booklover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14328604-aurian-booklover"><img alt="Aurian Booklover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352231803p2/14328604.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592919889?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aurian Booklover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aurian Booklover" href="/user/show/14328604-aurian-booklover">Aurian Booklover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592919889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6068256602673698515">Lady Cassidy is visiting some of her people for the first time, and she is very nervous about it. The Shalador people have had the worst of it all, and they really need her the most. Their whole culture was outlawed by the previous Queens, and they were bound to live on Reservations that kept getting smaller and smaller. But some of their Queens and Priestesses have survived in the deepest secret, and it is not easy for them to trust a new and foreign Queen. So much of the old ways have been for</span>
  <span id="freeText6068256602673698515" style="display:none">Lady Cassidy is visiting some of her people for the first time, and she is very nervous about it. The Shalador people have had the worst of it all, and they really need her the most. Their whole culture was outlawed by the previous Queens, and they were bound to live on Reservations that kept getting smaller and smaller. But some of their Queens and Priestesses have survived in the deepest secret, and it is not easy for them to trust a new and foreign Queen. So much of the old ways have been forgotten, and Cassidy can show them what to do for the land and its people. How to use the Queens gift to make the crops grow faster and stronger and healthier. But the land is drained, and it almost takes all Cassidy has to offer before someone stops her. Cassidy really likes her time in Shalador, but the Court has to return to Grayhaven Mansion again. And there a really nasty surprise awaits Cassie.<br />Her old nemesis, Queen Kermilla has arrived, trying to get some money out of Cassidy. Kermilla is the Queen her whole old court left her for, and it appears as if they are regretting their choice. Kermilla is not fit to be a Queen, she is a spendthrift and totally selfish. And now she wants what Cassidy has, again. Cassidy sends her back home, and banishes her from her country, but Theran interferes with her decision by inviting Kermilla to stay as his personal guest. <br /><br />It doesn’t take long for Cassidy to want to run, she can’t bear to live with Kermilla in the same house again, and see her use her flirting ways on her Court. So when Ranon finds out she is ready to leave them, he takes her home to the Shalador preserve again. And there they set up Court, without Theran who is as happy as can be with the woman he considers a true Queen. But he is blind to her true nature, and only sees her beauty. In the end, he will have to make a very hard choice. <br />Not only the Court joins Cassie in Shalador, some of the landen families she met want to join them as well. Theran wants to set up Lady Kermilla as the new Queen of Dena Nehele, and they really do not want to live under her reign. She is already abusing her power as a Queen, shoplifting and threatening people. <br /><br />Cassie even asks Daemon to help with opening some shops in the small village that is her new home, and he agrees, and even loans her an amazing amount of money to use to rebuild her country and Court. The people start trusting Cassidy, and she even has a young Shalador Queen serving as her apprentice. And when she brings back their culture, embraces it, the Shalador people start to love her. <br /><br />But her first probational year of being the Queen of Dena Nehele is almost over, and they all know that Theran will break her Court. They need to find a solution, and fast. Or there will be a civil war …<br /><br /><br />I really loved watching them rebuild the village; make a community, a home. Gray has come into his own, and when he is finally healed enough to be Cassie’s lover, wow, that was such a great scene. I enjoyed all the new Scelties as well, and how they guard the village against all villains. <br />Theran got what he so richly deserves, stupid blind man, and I hope he learns his lesson. But he will never be a part of Cassidy’s Court again. <br />Cassie is such a great character, down to earth and with a big heart. She is an outstanding Queen, and she reunites her people. I loved the building of the trust between them, and all the new developments. And of course the new Scelties, and how they charge people money to do their work. <br /><br />So many great characters, such a vivid world building, I really wish I could go visit them, meet them all, and of course be a Dark Jeweled Lady myself. <br /><br />10 stars.<br /><br /><p><br />© 2013 Reviews by Aurian </p><br /><br />Full review on my blog, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.boeklogboek.blogspot.com">www.boeklogboek.blogspot.com</a> <br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196989067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196989067" />
    <a title="Grete" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4021281-grete"><img alt="Grete" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312953923p2/4021281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196989067?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grete" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grete" href="/user/show/4021281-grete">Grete</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176267-shalador-s-lady">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4021281-grete?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4021281-grete?shelf=owned-on-kindle">owned-on-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196989067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16551987339212158598">(Originally Read 26th April 2010)<br/><br/>In Dena Nehele, Theran Grayhaven continues to struggle as First Escort to Cassidy, the Rose Jewelled Queen. Only able to see her shortcomings he clashes with the rest of the court, unable to see what they see or experience the bond that called them to serve in the first place. When an unexpected and unwelcome visitor turns up at Grayhaven, Theran is startled to find he has that bond with her and believes he has found the Queen meant to rule, instead of Cassidy. C</span>
  <span id="freeText16551987339212158598" style="display:none">(Originally Read 26th April 2010)<br /><br />In Dena Nehele, Theran Grayhaven continues to struggle as First Escort to Cassidy, the Rose Jewelled Queen. Only able to see her shortcomings he clashes with the rest of the court, unable to see what they see or experience the bond that called them to serve in the first place. When an unexpected and unwelcome visitor turns up at Grayhaven, Theran is startled to find he has that bond with her and believes he has found the Queen meant to rule, instead of Cassidy. Cassidy is not happy and the rest of her first circle are outraged when they realise the history Cassidy and the feckless Kermilla have and instinctively move to protect their Queen. Theran wanted a Queen from Kaeleer who could teach them protocol and the old ways of the Blood, before Dorotea’s taint crushed so much of Terreille. He can’t accept that what he wants and what the territory needs are two different things. If he can’t accept Cassidy and her ruling, everything he wanted for Dena Nehele would be lost, including the land itself.<br /><br />I have nothing but love for any book or story set in the Black Jewels Universe. Right from Daughter of the Blood, the first book in the series I was hooked on the characters and the the rich dark world that the three realms made up. Yet another series I need to re-read and review as I go. I can’t recommend them highly enough, seriously! This review might be a little confusing if you’ve not read any of the books as the titles and terms are unique to Anne Bishop’s work. Another reason to read them!<br /><br />Shalador’s Lady follows straight on from The Shadow Queen and while sad, it wasn’t surprising that Theran couldn’t get his act together enough to realise that while Cassidy might not be the Queen he wanted, she was the Queen that Dena Nehele needed. It was a pleasure to witness Cassidy’s continued growth into a strong Queen and prove her ability to rule, despite the light jewels she wears. She is a great character and one who fits right in to the group of exceptional people I have come to love so much in these books.<br /><br />Theran was just plain irritating but his disappointment with Cassidy and his lack of the bond that the other males had meant I could understand where he was coming from. I still wanted to smack him a lot.<br /><br />Gray on the other hand was a joy, seeing his continued emergence from the damaged and scared boy trapped in an adult’s body into the Warlord Prince he should have been. Wow. The other Males of Cassidy’s First Circle were also great, stepping up to the line when needed and understanding that without Cassidy and bringing back the old ways of the Blood, there would be no more Dena Nehele.<br /><br />Finally comes those characters that I could read about forever. Daemon, Jaenelle, Saetan and Lucivar to name the top four. Other beloved character make appearances and it was truly great to see them. I have heard complaints that when it comes to stories in the Black Jewels Universe that aren’t directly about them, they still make appearances. I honestly don’t see how they can’t considering who they are and their place in the world. In my opinion there can’t be enough about them!<br /><br />The story I can’t actually touch on much as it would spoil it, but it was good and the plot unexpected at times. The pace flowed with Bishop’s usual grace and as always, I find her characterisations nothing short of amazing.<br /><br />In all, a fantastic book and a credit to the series and Anne Bishop.<br /><br />This review and others can also be read at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookthing.co.uk">http://www.bookthing.co.uk</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16551987339212158598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146295316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146295316" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4323315-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491595021p2/4323315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146295316?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4323315-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4323315-laura?shelf=beach-read">beach-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4323315-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146295316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4049757277145774348">Right off the bat, you ought to know I'm biased. I love, love, love Anne Bishop's Black Jewel's universe. The love affair began way back. I was making my usual preparations for the onset of a cold: grocery shopping for canned soups and jello and visiting the local bookstore for something light to read, fantasy, while I was bedbound. I wanted something new by an author I hadn't read before. And there she was: Anne Bishop. She had a whole trilogy ready for the reading. I took them home with a few </span>
  <span id="freeText4049757277145774348" style="display:none">Right off the bat, you ought to know I'm biased. I love, love, love Anne Bishop's Black Jewel's universe. The love affair began way back. I was making my usual preparations for the onset of a cold: grocery shopping for canned soups and jello and visiting the local bookstore for something light to read, fantasy, while I was bedbound. I wanted something new by an author I hadn't read before. And there she was: Anne Bishop. She had a whole trilogy ready for the reading. I took them home with a few other authors (Charlaine Harris and Terry Pratchett) for a taste of something new.<br /><br />As soon as I finished reading the Black Jewel's trilogy, I re-read the books. Each succeeding book has been no different. I've even developed a tradition for reading a new Black Jewels book. I read the series in sequence. Each book still has the ability to make me bounce in bed, cry, and smile while reading. The characters are true and the setting rich.<br /><br />Although Janelle and Daemon aren't the focal characters, they remain prominent in the storyline. Their marriage has matured. Lucivar and Saetan and even Tersa make their appearances with their usual senses of humor.<br /><br />"Shalador's Lady" focuses on rebuilding the ruins created by Janelle's great unbinding and unloosing of two years prior. Landen and blood are still at odds with each other but in the building of a new society they work out a truce and even learn how to live with each other.<br /><br />"Shalador's Lady" is a rebuilding, too, of Gray. He, too, was broken by the witches/bitches. He's ready (and eager) to take on his role of man and warrior prince.<br /><br />Who inspires all this building? Cassidy, a plain, freckled, Rose-jeweled witch. <br /><br />Which leads to one of my gripes about this book (and most other fantasy fiction). Cassidy is compared (unfavorably) to a horse. Not even a thoroughbred horse with sleek lines but a bulky, clumsy drafthorse. Why, oh, why does the cover show a pretty young girl with nary a freckle in sight? If the heroine is an ordinary (even plain) young woman, why does the cover depict something else?<br /><br />I would not recommend any of Anne Bishop's books for any one under the age of 18. I would not recommend "Shalador's Lady" to anyone who hasn't read any of the other Black Jewel books. The Black Jewel universe is beautiful, lush, and well-developed. You need to know the background of the society before you can do yourself, or the books, justice.<br /><br />For those of you who were turned off by the graphic and sadistic scenes in the Black Jewels trilogy, Cassidy's books are much, much cleaner. Cassidy's books focus on courtship and hard work. The witch bitches are gone and so is the need to detail their sadistic practices.<br /><br />I eagerly await the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4049757277145774348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_193011804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193011804" />
    <a title="Theresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1229058-theresa"><img alt="Theresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323811101p2/1229058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193011804?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa" href="/user/show/1229058-theresa">Theresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193011804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1307900933623146548">Over ten years ago Anne Bishop's first entry in the <a href='http://www.amazon.com/s/ref=nb_sb_noss?url=search-alias%3Dus-stripbooks-tree&field-keywords=black+jewels+trilogy&x=0&y=0' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black Jewels trilogy</a> was released and many readers were captivated by her rich fantasy that cast Saetan, the High Lord of Hell, as a heroic character. But time has mellowed Bishop's characters and <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Shaladors-Lady-Black-Jewels-Novel/dp/0451463153/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&s=books&qid=1269238390&sr=1-1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shalador's Lady</a>, the eighth book in Bishop's Black Jewels series, reads more like a Harlequin Romance than a dark fantasy.<br/><br/>The Black Jewels series is based on a unique mythology that uses familiar names from The Bible-- though they are given their own </span>
  <span id="freeText1307900933623146548" style="display:none">Over ten years ago Anne Bishop's first entry in the <a href="http://www.amazon.com/s/ref=nb_sb_noss?url=search-alias%3Dus-stripbooks-tree&amp;field-keywords=black+jewels+trilogy&amp;x=0&amp;y=0" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Jewels trilogy</a> was released and many readers were captivated by her rich fantasy that cast Saetan, the High Lord of Hell, as a heroic character. But time has mellowed Bishop's characters and <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Shaladors-Lady-Black-Jewels-Novel/dp/0451463153/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;s=books&amp;qid=1269238390&amp;sr=1-1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shalador's Lady</a>, the eighth book in Bishop's Black Jewels series, reads more like a Harlequin Romance than a dark fantasy.<br /><br />The Black Jewels series is based on a unique mythology that uses familiar names from The Bible-- though they are given their own twist for this particular fantasy. The original series followed the story of Saetan, his sons Daemon and Lucivar, and Jaenelle-- the most powerful Queen to ever live-- also known as Witch. The society is caste based and much of the hierarchy is drawn from the jewels each witch or warlord wears in addition to their birth rank. The original trilogy was a dark, Gothic fantasy that could be both violent and romantic. But once the story reached its climax, it also lost most of its tension.<br /><br />"Shalador's Lady," the eighth book in the series, is the second book the follow the story of Lady Cassidy; a light jeweled Queen who has been chosen to rule the land of Dena Nehele. Cassidy has never been a powerful Queen and suffered the abandonment of her first court due to the machinations of a younger, darker jeweled Queen. And though she has settled into a new life in Dena Nehele, she doesn't have the full support of Theran Greyhaven, the heir to the territory she currently rules. And when a former rival shows up unexpectedly, Cassidy is sure she will be abandoned by her court once again.<br /><br />There isn't a lot of real excitement or drama to "Shalador's Lady." It's a sweet book with likable characters, but it's like a "light" version of the original series. Many of the same characters are brought back, including Saetan, Daemon and Jaenelle, but you get the feeling that they're really there for nostalgia's sake. In fact, the whole book seems to have been written for the fans, and perhaps the author, who are loathe to leave the world Bishop created. Most of the book is taken up with a series of minor misunderstandings and manufactured drama just so we can see Cassidy finally have her happy ending. It's fun to revisit old characters, but I miss the bite of the earlier books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1307900933623146548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132453081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132453081" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2950473-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365040504p2/2950473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132453081?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/2950473-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101185889" href="/book/show/7880997-shalador-s-lady">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2950473-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer132453081&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132453081" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14043073574625466142">I found this book to be a very satisfying continuation of Lady Cassidy's story from The Shadow Queen (Black Jewels, Book 7). Even though a Bishop wields a substantial cast of characters between the pages of this book, each character is given his or her time in the spotlight, from my series favorites, such as Surreal and Daemon, to newer characters like Gray and Ranon. Each one has a subplot to work through, yet all loose ends are resolved quite neatly. I enjoyed how the plot would switch seamles</span>
  <span id="freeText14043073574625466142" style="display:none">I found this book to be a very satisfying continuation of Lady Cassidy's story from The Shadow Queen (Black Jewels, Book 7). Even though a Bishop wields a substantial cast of characters between the pages of this book, each character is given his or her time in the spotlight, from my series favorites, such as Surreal and Daemon, to newer characters like Gray and Ranon. Each one has a subplot to work through, yet all loose ends are resolved quite neatly. I enjoyed how the plot would switch seamlessly between the story arcs of Cassidy's realm and Jaenelle's realm without taking away from either.<br /><br />This book seemed to give the reader a glimpse into how the tainting of the Blood occurred by how good men could become bound to bad Queens. Kermilla played the role perfectly by how naive and self-centered she behaved, making her completely oblivious to the trouble she was creating. It is easy to see what Theran sees in her, because it is clear to me that were she to ever learn to use her strengths for the good of others instead of herself, she could become a very powerful force. Though I could not stand Kermilla from the very beginning, I think her character has too much potential not to use her in further books in the Black Jewels series.<br /><br />The Kindred of the Blood continue to take a vital role in the progression of the plot, which I find both ingenious and quite humorous, as they are unpredictable in many ways. With the Kindred involved, there is guaranteed to be surprises - both good and bad. I could easily see a Kindred-centered novella come out of this book.<br /><br />My favorite part of this book was watching the transformation of Gray into Jared Blaed as him and Cassidy fall in love. The progression is slow without feeling dragged out, and each stage has its rewards, with his casual relationship with Jaenelle's inner circle, as well as his introduction into Cassidy's circle. I'm a bit disappointed that Bishop did not create a way for Gray to gain the power he missed out on the first time, simply because it feels like he was punished for what he had no control over in his past.<br /><br />I also love the humor that Bishop interjects so effortlessly into the plot, such as the interactions between Ranon and Gray and the rest of Jaenelle's court. The same old chemistry is still there with all of the "former court," and I have to wonder if the references to her court don't indicate a coming change in future books. I greatly look forward to the next installment in the Black Jewels series, Twilight's Dawn: A Black Jewels Book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14043073574625466142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_561375127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561375127" />
    <a title="Ginger Vampyre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614258-ginger-vampyre"><img alt="Ginger Vampyre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307835549p2/5614258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561375127?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger Vampyre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger Vampyre" href="/user/show/5614258-ginger-vampyre">Ginger Vampyre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561375127" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16597453435716794950">A continuation of The Shadow Queen, Cassidy ruling Dena Nehele in Terreille, trying to restore the Old Ways of the Blood and heal a land torn by war and abuse. Theran continues to hobble Cassidy's efforts at restoring Dena Nehele. He has his own ideas about what, and who, is important and Cassidy treating the Shalador people like equals, deserving of what she can give them same as the others, bothers him. He views it has another way Cassidy is a disappointment to his people. Except that he conti</span>
  <span id="freeText16597453435716794950" style="display:none">A continuation of The Shadow Queen, Cassidy ruling Dena Nehele in Terreille, trying to restore the Old Ways of the Blood and heal a land torn by war and abuse. Theran continues to hobble Cassidy's efforts at restoring Dena Nehele. He has his own ideas about what, and who, is important and Cassidy treating the Shalador people like equals, deserving of what she can give them same as the others, bothers him. He views it has another way Cassidy is a disappointment to his people. Except that he continues to be the only person who sees her that way. Another Queen from Kaeleer comes to visit, Kermilla, the queen who took Cassidy's court. She wants a gift of tithe from Cassidy for taking over her territory in Kaeleer because she has already spent all of the tithes from the people. But having Kermilla in Dena Nehele is is shaking Cassidy's confidence. Theran has decided that Kermilla is his Queen and defies Cassidy in allowing her to stay at Grayhaven and Cassidy starts thinking that the rest of her court will follow. Cassidy decides to leave before her court leaves her, but as she is packing she is caught by Ranon who takes her back to his people. A place that she feels safe and where every one is grateful to her as a Queen and as a person. With the sole exception of Theran her court follows her to the Shalador reservation and they all decide to rule from there rather than return to Grayhaven. While Theran remains at Greyhaven and tries to teach Kermilla what she would know to rule Dena Nehele, Kermilla complains about the lack of proper aristo and that Theran is holding back on the money she should have to shop as a Queen should. A division starts to grow between the two camps, between two ways of being a Queen. This division leads to provinces breaking off from Dena Nehele and creating a new territory, a territory that chooses Cassidy as its Queen.</span>

<div id="review_106579566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106579566" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1366121-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106579566?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/1366121-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106579566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10518656138095959379">Well, Anne Bishop has done it again. Another delightful tale of the Blood that's completely engaging and hard to put down, seasoned generously with the heart and wit that make these books so charming. This tome follows the tale of Cassidy, who we met in 'The Shadow Queen,' as she contines to try and rule her demense. Alas, all is not well within her court, and even as she continues to improve the land, she is betrayed from within. Will she falter, or find the strength to overcome the opposition?</span>
  <span id="freeText10518656138095959379" style="display:none">Well, Anne Bishop has done it again. Another delightful tale of the Blood that's completely engaging and hard to put down, seasoned generously with the heart and wit that make these books so charming. This tome follows the tale of Cassidy, who we met in 'The Shadow Queen,' as she contines to try and rule her demense. Alas, all is not well within her court, and even as she continues to improve the land, she is betrayed from within. Will she falter, or find the strength to overcome the opposition?<br /><br />I will say this: the book is about 90% pure politics. Generally I loathe such tomes (WoT suffers greatly from this problem in parts), but her characters! The characters are just so likeable, she actually makes politics interesting. <br /><br />I think its the fact that her characters are just so human, yet more, at the same time, that makes them so attractive. They glare, they loom dangerously, they spout vast quantities of energy, they speak in spooky voices. But at the same time, they make idiots of themselves, they get all snarly, they bitch and moan. And no one's exempt. Everyone, even the most mighty, is at some point a fool. And that makes the characters so much more believable. <br /><br />All the characters do a lot of growing and developing in this book - in particular Gray. Also, there is quite a large Sceltie presence in this chapter of the 'Jewels' saga. It adds quite a bit of lighthearted fun.<br /><br />I found the resolution to be both satisfying and amusing. Not much action in the volume, but a great deal of character growth and major world developments. Not a book you'd want to introduce someone 'Black Jewels' with, but a fun and enjoyable read for fans of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10518656138095959379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106987777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106987777" />
    <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites"><img alt="Lisa (Harmonybites)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337396485p2/2596042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106987777?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa (Harmonybites)" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites">Lisa (Harmonybites)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Bishop's Dark Jewels Books</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106987777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1109968342084995619">If you haven't read another novel in Bishop's Dark Jewels universe, this wouldn't be where I'd start. Go read the opening trilogy in the series first, which starts with <i>Daughter of the Blood</i>, since this novel would act as a spoiler, and those are the strongest novels in the series. You'd also want to read <i>The Shadow Queen</i> before reading this novel, since <i>Shalador's Lady</i> is the sequel, and I think you'd be lost without reading it. (<i>The Invisible Ring</i>, which is set a few hundred years before, also</span>
  <span id="freeText1109968342084995619" style="display:none">If you haven't read another novel in Bishop's Dark Jewels universe, this wouldn't be where I'd start. Go read the opening trilogy in the series first, which starts with <i>Daughter of the Blood</i>, since this novel would act as a spoiler, and those are the strongest novels in the series. You'd also want to read <i>The Shadow Queen</i> before reading this novel, since <i>Shalador's Lady</i> is the sequel, and I think you'd be lost without reading it. (<i>The Invisible Ring</i>, which is set a few hundred years before, also provides backstory, but I don't think is crucial to be read before this one). <br /><br />If you have read and enjoyed <i>The Shadow Queen</i> however, you won't be disappointed, in fact I think this is the stronger novel, which strikes a better balance between the parts of the book that checks in with Jaenelle and other characters from earlier in the series and Cassidy and her court. <br /><br />I could pick at some flaws. I think Kermilla makes a weak antagonist, vapid and shallow--I couldn't understand either Theron's attraction or Cassidy's panic at her rival's appearance, especially after all they'd been through together, and what I had thought Theron had learned from the events of the last book. Both Theron and Cassidy at certain points acted in ways that made me want to slap them, and wonder why they've seemingly regressed. <br /><br />Nevertheless, this story more than once moved me to laughter and even tears, and any novel that does that belongs among my favorites. (The pack of Scelties were a highlight.) And if you do love the Dark Jewels books, it's like settling down to catch up with old friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1109968342084995619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>

</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oq2dX+r0DuIoHbSZpQ3HycAYMCd6vorgQIwSHNFgIBnA46xJRa6G26OuluyMqpMFnwF3XkcQ7lr0SG84fi7FdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9cEnpYqIWDkcUtkQNFvEdi3MIrsK3qFQm6S2E712lKGXjxazJdLQAJfh+2Ud/JC6ctVlwjdwxeovYMs3EjhxzA==')})
  }

</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3545500165387191306">Anne Bishop lives in upstate New York where she enjoys gardening, music, and writing dark, romantic stories. She is the author of over twenty novels, including the award-winning Black Jewels Trilogy. She has written a new series, the Others, which is an urban dark fantasy with a bit of a twist.<br/><br/>Crawford Award (2000)<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this na</i></span>

    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
